<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hundred_Years%27_War_(1415%E2%80%931453)" title="Hundred Years' War (1415–1453)">Hundred Years' War (1415–1453)</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Burgundy_alliance_and_the_taking_of_Paris">Burgundy alliance and the taking of Paris</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hundred_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Burgundy alliance and the taking of Paris">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Battle_of_Agincourt_.281415.29">Battle of Agincourt (1415)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hundred_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Battle of Agincourt (1415)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Agincourt" title="Battle of Agincourt">Battle of Agincourt</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Agincour.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1249" data-file-width="1500" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Agincour.JPG/220px-Agincour.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Agincour.JPG/330px-Agincour.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Agincour.JPG/440px-Agincour.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Agincour.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Fifteenth-century miniature depicting the Battle of Agincourt.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In August 1415, <a href="/wiki/Henry_V_of_England" title="Henry V of England">Henry V</a> sailed from England with a force of about 10,500 and laid siege to <a href="/wiki/Harfleur" title="Harfleur">Harfleur</a>. The city resisted for longer than expected, but finally surrendered on 22 September 1415. Because of the unexpected delay, most of the campaign season was gone. Rather than march on Paris directly, Henry elected to make a raiding expedition across France toward English-occupied Calais. In a campaign reminiscent of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cr%C3%A9cy" title="Crécy">Crécy</a>, he found himself outmaneuvered and low on supplies and had to fight a much larger French army at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Agincourt" title="Battle of Agincourt">Battle of Agincourt</a>, north of the <a href="/wiki/Somme_(river)" title="Somme (river)">Somme</a>. Despite the problems and having a smaller force, his victory was near-total; the French defeat was catastrophic, costing the lives of many of the Armagnac leaders. About 40% of the French nobility was killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-population-60">[60]</a></sup> Henry was apparently concerned that the large number of prisoners taken were a security risk (there were more French prisoners than there were soldiers in the entire English army) and he ordered their deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dnballmand_59-2"><a href="#cite_note-dnballmand-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Treaty_of_Troyes_.281420.29">Treaty of Troyes (1420)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hundred_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Treaty of Troyes (1420)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Troyes" title="Treaty of Troyes">Treaty of Troyes</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Clan_member_crest_badge_-_Clan_Carmichael.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1123" data-file-width="884" height="279" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Clan_member_crest_badge_-_Clan_Carmichael.svg/220px-Clan_member_crest_badge_-_Clan_Carmichael.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Clan_member_crest_badge_-_Clan_Carmichael.svg/330px-Clan_member_crest_badge_-_Clan_Carmichael.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Clan_member_crest_badge_-_Clan_Carmichael.svg/440px-Clan_member_crest_badge_-_Clan_Carmichael.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Clan_member_crest_badge_-_Clan_Carmichael.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Clan_Carmichael" title="Clan Carmichael">Clan Carmichael</a> crest with broken spear commemorating the unseating of the Duke of Clarence.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Henry retook much of Normandy, including Caen in 1417, and <a href="/wiki/Rouen" title="Rouen">Rouen</a> on 19 January 1419, turning Normandy English for the first time in two centuries. A formal alliance was made with the Duchy of Burgundy, which had taken Paris after the assassination of Duke <a href="/wiki/John_the_Fearless" title="John the Fearless">John the Fearless</a> in 1419. In 1420, Henry met with King Charles VI. They signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Troyes" title="Treaty of Troyes">Treaty of Troyes</a>, by which Henry finally married Charles' daughter Catherine of Valois and Henry's heirs would inherit the throne of France. The Dauphin, <a href="/wiki/Charles_VII_of_France" title="Charles VII of France">Charles VII</a>, was declared illegitimate. Henry formally entered Paris later that year and the agreement was ratified by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_States-General" title="French States-General">Estates-General</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dnballmand_59-3"><a href="#cite_note-dnballmand-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_of_Clarence_.281421.29">Death of Clarence (1421)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hundred_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Death of Clarence (1421)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 22 March 1421 Henry V's progress in his French campaign experienced an unexpected reverse. Henry had left his brother and presumptive heir <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thomas,_Duke_of_Clarence" title="Thomas, Duke of Clarence">Thomas, Duke of Clarence</a> in charge while he returned to England. Clarence engaged a Franco-Scottish force of 5000 men, led by <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Motier_de_La_Fayette" title="Gilbert Motier de La Fayette">Gilbert Motier de La Fayette</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Stewart,_Earl_of_Buchan" title="John Stewart, Earl of Buchan">John Stewart, Earl of Buchan</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Baug%C3%A9" title="Battle of Baugé">Battle of Baugé</a>. Clarence, against the advice of his lieutenants, before his army had been fully assembled, attacked with a force of no more than 1500 men-at-arms. He then, during the course of the battle, led a charge of a few hundred men into the main body of the Franco-Scottish army, who quickly enveloped the English. In the ensuing melée, the Scot, John Carmichael of Douglasdale, broke his lance unhorsing the Duke of Clarence. Once on the ground, the duke was slain by <a href="/wiki/Sir_Alexander_Buchanan" title="Sir Alexander Buchanan">Alexander Buchanan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dnballmand_59-4"><a href="#cite_note-dnballmand-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wagner44_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-wagner44-61">[61]</a></sup> The body of the Duke of Clarence was recovered from the field by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thomas_Montacute,_4th_Earl_of_Salisbury" title="Thomas Montacute, 4th Earl of Salisbury">Thomas Montacute, 4th Earl of Salisbury</a>, who conducted the English retreat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-harris_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-harris-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="English_success">English success</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hundred_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: English success">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Henry V returned to France and went to Paris, then visiting Chartres and Gâtinais before returning to Paris. From there he decided to attack the Dauphin-held town of <a href="/wiki/Meaux" title="Meaux">Meaux</a>. It turned out to be more difficult to overcome than first thought. The siege began about 6 October 1421, and the town held for seven months before finally falling on 11 May 1422.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dnballmand_59-5"><a href="#cite_note-dnballmand-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the end of May, Henry was joined by his queen and together with the French court, they went to rest at <a href="/wiki/Senlis" title="Senlis">Senlis</a>. While there it became apparent that he was ill (possibly <a href="/wiki/Dysentery" title="Dysentery">dysentery</a>) and when he set out to the Upper Loire he diverted to the royal castle at Vincennes, near Paris, where he died on 31 August 1422.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dnballmand_59-6"><a href="#cite_note-dnballmand-59">[59]</a></sup> The elderly and insane Charles VI of France died two months later, on 21 October 1422. Henry left an only child, his nine-month-old son, <a href="/wiki/Henry_VI_of_England" title="Henry VI of England">Henry</a>, later to become Henry VI.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dnbgriffiths_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-dnbgriffiths-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>On his deathbed, Henry V had given the Duke of Bedford responsibility for English France (as Henry VI was only an infant). The war in France continued under Bedford's generalship and several battles were won. The English won an emphatic victory at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Verneuil" title="Battle of Verneuil">Battle of Verneuil</a>, (17 August 1424). At the Battle of Baugé, Clarence had rushed into battle without the support of his archers. At Verneuil the archers fought to devastating effect against the Franco-Scottish army. The effect of the battle was to virtually destroy the Dauphin's field army and to eliminate the Scots as a significant military force for the rest of the war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dnbgriffiths_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-dnbgriffiths-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wagner307_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-wagner307-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="French_victory:_1429.E2.80.9353">French victory: 1429–53</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hundred_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: French victory: 1429–53">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Joan_of_Arc_and_French_revival">Joan of Arc and French revival</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hundred_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Joan of Arc and French revival">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Joan_of_arc_miniature_graded.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1482" data-file-width="980" height="272" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Joan_of_arc_miniature_graded.jpg/180px-Joan_of_arc_miniature_graded.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Joan_of_arc_miniature_graded.jpg/270px-Joan_of_arc_miniature_graded.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Joan_of_arc_miniature_graded.jpg/360px-Joan_of_arc_miniature_graded.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Joan_of_arc_miniature_graded.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Joan_of_Arc" title="Joan of Arc">Joan of Arc</a> (c.1450–1500)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The appearance of <a href="/wiki/Joan_of_Arc" title="Joan of Arc">Joan of Arc</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Siege of Orléans">siege of Orléans</a> sparked a revival of French spirit, and the tide began to turn against the English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dnbgriffiths_63-2"><a href="#cite_note-dnbgriffiths-63">[63]</a></sup> The English laid <a href="/wiki/Siege" title="Siege">siege</a> to Orléans in 1428, but their force was insufficient to fully <a href="/wiki/Investment_(military)" title="Investment (military)">invest</a> the city. In 1429 Joan convinced the Dauphin to send her to the siege, saying she had received visions from God telling her to drive out the English. She raised the morale of the troops, and they attacked the English <a href="/wiki/Redoubt" title="Redoubt">redoubts</a>, forcing the English to lift the siege. Inspired by Joan, the French took several English strongholds on the Loire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-davis76_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-davis76-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>The English retreated from the Loire Valley, pursued by a French army. Near the village of <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Patay" title="Battle of Patay">Patay</a>, French cavalry broke through a unit of English longbowmen that had been sent to block the road, then swept through the retreating English army. The English lost 2,200 men, and the commander, <a href="/wiki/John_Talbot,_1st_Earl_of_Shrewsbury" title="John Talbot, 1st Earl of Shrewsbury">John Talbot, 1st Earl of Shrewsbury</a>, was taken prisoner. This victory opened the way for the Dauphin to march to <a href="/wiki/Reims" title="Reims">Reims</a> for his coronation as Charles VII, on 16 July 1429.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-davis76_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-davis76-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrofast_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-nrofast-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the coronation, Charles VII's army fared less well. An attempted French <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Paris_(1429)" title="Siege of Paris (1429)">siege of Paris</a> was defeated on 8 September 1429, and Charles VII withdrew to the Loire Valley.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Henry.27s_coronations_and_the_desertion_of_Burgundy">Henry's coronations and the desertion of Burgundy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hundred_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Henry's coronations and the desertion of Burgundy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Henry_VI_of_England" title="Henry VI of England">Henry VI</a> was crowned king of England at Westminster Abbey on 5 November 1429 and king of France at Notre-Dame, in Paris, on 16 December 1431.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dnbgriffiths_63-3"><a href="#cite_note-dnbgriffiths-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Siege_orleans.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1081" data-file-width="1382" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Siege_orleans.jpg/200px-Siege_orleans.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Siege_orleans.jpg/300px-Siege_orleans.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Siege_orleans.jpg/400px-Siege_orleans.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Siege_orleans.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The first Western image of a battle with cannon: the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siege_of_Orleans" title="Siege of Orleans">Siege of Orléans</a> in 1429.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Joan of Arc was captured by the Burgundians at the siege of Compiegne on 23 May 1430. The Burgundians transferred her to the English, who organised a trial headed by <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Cauchon" title="Pierre Cauchon">Pierre Cauchon</a>, Bishop of Beauvais and member of the English Council at Rouen. Joan was convicted and burned at the stake on 30 May 1431.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-davis76_65-2"><a href="#cite_note-davis76-65">[65]</a></sup> (She was rehabilitated 25 years later by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Callixtus_III" title="Pope Callixtus III">Pope Callixtus III</a>).</p>
<p>After the death of Joan of Arc, the fortunes of war turned dramatically against the English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lee145_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-lee145-68">[68]</a></sup> Most of Henry's royal advisers were against making peace. Among the factions, the Duke of Bedford wanted to defend Normandy, the Duke of Gloucester was committed to just Calais, whereas <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardinal_Beaufort" title="Cardinal Beaufort">Cardinal Beaufort</a> was inclined to peace. Negotiations stalled. It seems that at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Arras_(1435)" title="Treaty of Arras (1435)">congress of Arras</a>, in the summer of 1435, where the duke of Beaufort was mediator, the English were unrealistic in their demands. A few days after the congress ended in September, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philip_III,_duke_of_Burgundy" title="Philip III, duke of Burgundy">Philip III, duke of Burgundy</a>, deserted to Charles VII, signing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Arras_(1435)" title="Treaty of Arras (1435)">Treaty of Arras</a> that returned Paris to the King of France. This was a major blow to English sovereignty in France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dnbgriffiths_63-4"><a href="#cite_note-dnbgriffiths-63">[63]</a></sup> The Duke of Bedford died on 14 September 1435 and was replaced by a lesser man.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lee145_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-lee145-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_resurgence">French resurgence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hundred_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: French resurgence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vigiles_du_roi_Charles_VII_32.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="426" data-file-width="530" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Vigiles_du_roi_Charles_VII_32.jpg/220px-Vigiles_du_roi_Charles_VII_32.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Vigiles_du_roi_Charles_VII_32.jpg/330px-Vigiles_du_roi_Charles_VII_32.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Vigiles_du_roi_Charles_VII_32.jpg/440px-Vigiles_du_roi_Charles_VII_32.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vigiles_du_roi_Charles_VII_32.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Battle of Formigny (1450)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The allegiance of Burgundy remained fickle, but the English focus on expanding their domains in the Low Countries left them little energy to intervene in the rest of France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sumption562_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-sumption562-69">[69]</a></sup> The long truces that marked the war gave Charles time to centralise the French state and reorganise his army and government, replacing his feudal levies with a more modern professional army that could put its superior numbers to good use. A castle that once could only be captured after a prolonged siege would now fall after a few days from cannon bombardment. The French artillery developed a reputation as the best in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lee145_68-2"><a href="#cite_note-lee145-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 1449, the French had retaken <a href="/wiki/Rouen" title="Rouen">Rouen</a>. In 1450 the <a href="/wiki/Counts_of_Clermont-en-Beauvaisis" title="Counts of Clermont-en-Beauvaisis">Count of Clermont</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arthur_III,_Duke_of_Brittany" title="Arthur III, Duke of Brittany">Arthur de Richemont</a>, Earl of Richmond, of the Montfort family (the future <a href="/wiki/Arthur_III,_Duke_of_Brittany" title="Arthur III, Duke of Brittany">Arthur III, Duke of Brittany</a>), caught an English army attempting to relieve Caen and defeated it at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Formigny" title="Battle of Formigny">Battle of Formigny</a>. Richemont's force attacked the English army from the flank and rear just as they were on the verge of beating Clermont's army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nicole26_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-nicole26-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fall_of_Gascony">Fall of Gascony</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hundred_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Fall of Gascony">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Charles_VII_by_Jean_Fouquet_1445_1450.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="504" height="262" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Charles_VII_by_Jean_Fouquet_1445_1450.jpg/220px-Charles_VII_by_Jean_Fouquet_1445_1450.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Charles_VII_by_Jean_Fouquet_1445_1450.jpg/330px-Charles_VII_by_Jean_Fouquet_1445_1450.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Charles_VII_by_Jean_Fouquet_1445_1450.jpg/440px-Charles_VII_by_Jean_Fouquet_1445_1450.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Charles_VII_by_Jean_Fouquet_1445_1450.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Charles_VII_of_France" title="Charles VII of France">Charles "the Victorious"</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After Charles VII's successful Normandy campaign in 1450, he concentrated his efforts on Gascony, the last province held by the English. Bordeaux, Gascony's capital, was besieged and surrendered to the French on 30 June 1451. Largely due to the English sympathies of the Gascon people, this was reversed when John Talbot and his army retook the city on 23 October 1452. However, the English were decisively defeated at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Castillon" title="Battle of Castillon">Battle of Castillon</a> on 17 July 1453. Talbot had been persuaded to engage the French army at Castillon near Bordeaux. During the battle the French appeared to retreat towards their camp. The French camp at Castillon had been laid out by Charles VII's ordnance officer <a href="/wiki/Jean_Bureau" title="Jean Bureau">Jean Bureau</a> and this was instrumental in the French success as when the French cannon opened fire, from their positions in the camp, the English took severe casualties losing both Talbot and his son.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wagner79_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-wagner79-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="End_of_the_war">End of the war</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hundred_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: End of the war">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Although the Battle of Castillon is considered the last battle of the Hundred Years' War,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wagner79_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-wagner79-71">[71]</a></sup> England and France remained formally at war for another 20 years, but the English were in no position to carry on the war as they faced unrest at home. Following defeat in the Hundred Years' War, English landowners complained vociferously about the financial losses resulting from the loss of their continental holdings; this is often considered a major cause of the <a href="/wiki/Wars_of_the_Roses" title="Wars of the Roses">Wars of the Roses</a>, that started in 1455.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lee145_68-3"><a href="#cite_note-lee145-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-webster39_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-webster39-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<div aria-labelledby="Burgundian_Wars_.281474.E2.80.9377.29" class="navbox" role="navigation" style="margin:0;float:right;clear:right;width:315px;margin-bottom:0.5em;margin-left:1em;;padding:3px">
<table class="nowraplinks collapsible autocollapse navbox-inner" style="border-spacing:0;background:transparent;color:inherit">
<tr>
<th class="navbox-title" colspan="2" scope="col" style="background-color:#B0C4DE;">
<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
<ul>
<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Campaignbox_Burgundian_Wars" title="Template:Campaignbox Burgundian Wars"><abbr style=";background-color:#B0C4DE;;background:none transparent;border:none;" title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Campaignbox_Burgundian_Wars" title="Template talk:Campaignbox Burgundian Wars"><abbr style=";background-color:#B0C4DE;;background:none transparent;border:none;" title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Campaignbox_Burgundian_Wars&amp;action=edit"><abbr style=";background-color:#B0C4DE;;background:none transparent;border:none;" title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
</ul>
</div>
<div id="Burgundian_Wars_.281474.E2.80.9377.29" style="font-size:114%"><span style="line-height:1.6em"><a href="/wiki/Burgundian_Wars" title="Burgundian Wars">Burgundian Wars</a> (1474–77)</span></div>
</th>
</tr>
<tr style="height:2px">
<td colspan="2"></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" colspan="2" style="width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Neuss" title="Siege of Neuss">Neuss</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_H%C3%A9ricourt" title="Battle of Héricourt">Héricourt</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_on_the_Planta" title="Battle on the Planta">Planta</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Grandson" title="Battle of Grandson">Grandson</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Morat" title="Battle of Morat">Morat</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nancy" title="Battle of Nancy">Nancy</a></li>
</ul>
<hr/>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Guinegate_(1479)" title="Battle of Guinegate (1479)">Guinegate</a></li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
</div>
<p>The Hundred Years' War almost resumed in 1474, when the duke <a href="/wiki/Charles_the_Bold" title="Charles the Bold">Charles of Burgundy</a>, counting on English support, <a href="/wiki/Burgundian_Wars" title="Burgundian Wars">took up arms</a> against <a href="/wiki/Louis_XI_of_France" title="Louis XI of France">Louis XI of France</a>. Louis managed to isolate the Burgundians by buying <a href="/wiki/Edward_IV_of_England" title="Edward IV of England">Edward IV of England</a> off with a large cash sum and an annual pension, in an agreement signed at the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Picquigny" title="Treaty of Picquigny">Treaty of Picquigny</a> (1475). The treaty formally ended the Hundred Years' War with Edward renouncing his claim to the throne of France. However, future Kings of England (and later of Great Britain) continued to <a href="/wiki/English_claims_to_the_French_throne" title="English claims to the French throne">claim the title</a> until 1803, when they were dropped in deference to the exiled Count of Provence, titular King <a href="/wiki/Louis_XVIII_of_France" title="Louis XVIII of France">Louis XVIII of France</a>, who was living in England after the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-neillands290_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-neillands290-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>Charles the Bold, the last duke of Burgundy, was killed at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nancy" title="Battle of Nancy">Battle of Nancy</a> in 1477,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ross249-250_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ross249-250-74">[74]</a></sup> leaving a daughter, <a href="/wiki/Mary_of_Burgundy" title="Mary of Burgundy">Mary</a>, who lost the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Artois" title="Artois">Artois</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_of_Flanders" title="County of Flanders">Flanders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Picardy" title="Picardy">Picardy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burgundy" title="Burgundy">Burgundy</a> to Louis XI's armies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ross249-250_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ross249-250-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Significance">Significance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hundred_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Significance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_France_1477-en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="970" data-file-width="900" height="237" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Map_France_1477-en.svg/220px-Map_France_1477-en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Map_France_1477-en.svg/330px-Map_France_1477-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Map_France_1477-en.svg/440px-Map_France_1477-en.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_France_1477-en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Burgundian territories (orange/yellow) and limits of France (red) after the Burgundian War.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_signifiance">Historical signifiance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hundred_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Historical signifiance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The French victory marked the end of a long period of instability that had started with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norman_Conquest" title="Norman Conquest">Norman Conquest</a> (1066), when <a href="/wiki/William_the_Conqueror" title="William the Conqueror">William the Conqueror</a> added "King of England" to his titles, becoming both the vassal to (as Duke of Normandy) and the equal of (as king of England) the king of France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>When the war ended, England was bereft of its Continental possessions (with the exception of the <a href="/wiki/Pale_of_Calais" title="Pale of Calais">Pale of Calais</a>), leaving it on an island on the periphery of Europe, which greatly affected the English mind-set.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gregory_D._Cleva_p._87_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gregory_D._Cleva_p._87-1">[1]</a></sup> The war destroyed the English dream of a joint monarchy and led to the rejection in England of all things French, but the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Norman_language" title="Anglo-Norman language">French language in England</a>, which had served as the language of the ruling classes and commerce there from the time of the Norman conquest, left many vestiges in English vocabulary. English became the official language in 1362 and French was no longer used for teaching from 1385.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>National feeling that emerged from the war unified both France and England further. Despite the devastation on its soil, the Hundred Years' War accelerated the process of transforming France from a feudal monarchy to a centralised state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-holmes61_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-holmes61-77">[77]</a></sup> In England the political and financial troubles which emerged from the defeat was one major cause of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_of_the_Roses" title="War of the Roses">War of the Roses</a> (1455–1487).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bubonic_plague_map.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1108" data-file-width="1024" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Bubonic_plague_map.PNG/220px-Bubonic_plague_map.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Bubonic_plague_map.PNG/330px-Bubonic_plague_map.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Bubonic_plague_map.PNG/440px-Bubonic_plague_map.PNG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bubonic_plague_map.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The spread of the <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a> (with modern borders).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Lowe (1997) argued that opposition to the war helped to shape England's early modern political culture. Although anti-war and pro-peace spokesmen generally failed to influence outcomes at the time, they had a long-term impact. England showed decreasing enthusiasm for conflict deemed not in the national interest, yielding only losses in return for high economic burdens. In comparing this English cost-benefit analysis with French attitudes, given that both countries suffered from weak leaders and undisciplined soldiers, Lowe noted that the French understood that warfare was necessary to expel the foreigners occupying their homeland. Furthermore, French kings found alternative ways to finance the war – sales taxes, debasing the coinage – and were less dependent than the English on tax levies passed by national legislatures. English anti-war critics thus had more to work with than the French.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bubonic <a href="/wiki/Plague_(disease)" title="Plague (disease)">plague</a> and warfare reduced population numbers throughout Europe during this period. France lost half its population during the Hundred Years' War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-population-60">[60]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Normandy" title="Normandy">Normandy</a> lost three-quarters of its population, and Paris two-thirds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> The population of England was reduced by 20 to 33 percent due to plague in the same period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-neillands110_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-neillands110-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_signifiance">Military signifiance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hundred_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Military signifiance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1445 the first regular standing army in Western Europe since Roman times was organised in France partly as a solution to marauding free companies. The mercenary companies were given a choice of either joining the Royal army as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Compagnies_d%27ordonnance" title="Compagnies d'ordonnance">compagnies d'ordonnance</a> on a permanent basis, or being hunted down and destroyed if they refused. France gained a total standing army of around 6,000 men, which was sent out to gradually eliminate the remaining mercenaries who insisted on operating on their own. The new standing army had a more disciplined and professional approach to warfare than its predecessors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RolandPreston1991_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-RolandPreston1991-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Hundred Years' War was a time of rapid military evolution. Weapons, tactics, army structure and the social meaning of war all changed, partly in response to the war's costs, partly through advancement in technology and partly through lessons that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Warfare" title="Warfare">warfare</a> taught. The feudal system was slowly disintegrating throughout the hundred years war.</p>
<p>By the war's end, although the heavy cavalry was still considered the most powerful unit in an army, the heavy horse had to deal with several tactics developed to deny or mitigate its effective use on a battlefield.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-powicke189_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-powicke189-83">[83]</a></sup> The English began using lightly armoured mounted troops, known as <a href="/wiki/Hobelar" title="Hobelar">hobelars</a>. Hobelars tactics had been developed against the Scots, in the Anglo-Scottish wars of the 14th century. Hobelars rode smaller unarmoured horses, enabling them to move through difficult or boggy terrain where heavier cavalry would struggle. Rather than fight while seated on the horse, they would dismount to engage the enemy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RolandPreston1991_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-RolandPreston1991-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rogers267_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-rogers267-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jonesr1_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-jonesr1-85">[85]</a></sup></p>

<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_Hundred_Years%27_War" title="Timeline of the Hundred Years' War">Timeline of the Hundred Years' War</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_military_history" title="French military history">French military history</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_military_history" title="British military history">British military history</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglo-French_relations" title="Anglo-French relations">Anglo-French relations</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Medieval_demography" title="Medieval demography">Medieval demography</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Second_Hundred_Years%27_War" title="Second Hundred Years' War">Second Hundred Years' War</a>- this is the name given by some historians to the near-continuous series of conflicts between Britain and France from 1688 to 1815, beginning with the <a href="/wiki/Glorious_Revolution" title="Glorious Revolution">Glorious Revolution</a> and ending with the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Waterloo" title="Battle of Waterloo">Battle of Waterloo</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_battles_involving_France_in_the_Middle_Ages" title="List of battles involving France in the Middle Ages">List of battles involving France in the Middle Ages</a></li>
</ul>
